Contains the view function, args, kwargs, url_name, namespaces, app_names, route information, and captured kwargs.\\n\\n## URL Resolution & Reverse Lookup (django/urls/base.py)\\nThe resolve() function (line 22) takes a URL path and resolves it to a view, accepting an optional urlconf parameter. It calls get_resolver().resolve(path).\\n\\nThe reverse() function (line 28) does the opposite, taking a view name and kwargs to generate the corresponding URL path. It supports nested namespaces and query parameters.\\n\\n## Main Exports (django/urls/__init__.py)\\nThe django.urls module exports all public API: path, re_path, include from conf.py; URLPattern, URLResolver, ResolverMatch, LocalePrefixPattern from resolvers.py; resolve, reverse, and other utilities from base.py.\\n\\n## Internationalization (django/conf/urls/i18n.py)\\nThe i18n_patterns() function (line 8) wraps URL patterns with a LocalePrefixPattern URLResolver to add language code prefixes. The is_language_prefix_patterns_used() function (line 24) checks if i18n_patterns() was applied to a URLconf.\\n\\n## Historical Context\\nThe patterns() function that created URL pattern lists was removed in Django 1.10 (mentioned in docs/releases/1.10.txt line 1228). The modern approach uses plain Python lists of path()/re_path() calls assigned to urlpatterns, with include() to nest configurations and URLResolver to handle the nesting internally.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
